<td style="padding:2px;">
<h2 id="mp-tfa-h2" style="margin:3px; background:#cef2e0; font-family:inherit; font-size:120%; font-weight:bold; border:1px solid #a3bfb1; text-align:left; color:#000; padding:0.2em 0.4em;"><span class="mw-headline" id="From_today.27s_featured_article">From today's featured article</span></h2>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="color:#000;">
<div id="mp-tfa" style="padding:2px 5px">
<div id="mp-tfa-img" style="float: left; margin: 0.5em 0.9em 0.4em 0em;">
<div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Miller_ww2.jpg" title="Keith Miller in 1945"><img alt="Keith Miller in 1945" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Miller_ww2_%28cropped%29.jpg/100px-Miller_ww2_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="100" height="133" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Miller_ww2_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Miller_ww2_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Miller_ww2_%28cropped%29.jpg/200px-Miller_ww2_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="276" data-file-height="368" /></a></div>
</div>
<p>The Australian cricketer <a href="/wiki/Keith_Miller_with_the_Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1948" title="Keith Miller with the Australian cricket team in England in 1948"><b>Keith Miller toured England in 1948</b></a> as a member of <a href="/wiki/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1948" title="Australian cricket team in England in 1948">The Invincibles</a>, a team that went undefeated in their 34 tour matches. Miller (28 November 1919 – 11 October 2004) was an <a href="/wiki/All-rounder" title="All-rounder">all-rounder</a>: a <a href="/wiki/Fast_bowling" title="Fast bowling">fast bowler</a> and a right-handed <a href="/wiki/Batting_order_(cricket)" title="Batting order (cricket)">middle-order</a> <a href="/wiki/Batsman" class="mw-redirect" title="Batsman">batsman</a>. <a href="/wiki/Don_Bradman" title="Don Bradman">Don Bradman</a>, the team captain, typically used him and <a href="/wiki/Ray_Lindwall" title="Ray Lindwall">Ray Lindwall</a> in short bursts with the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball#Condition_of_a_cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">new ball</a>. Miller took 13 <a href="/wiki/Wicket" title="Wicket">wickets</a> at an <a href="/wiki/Bowling_average" title="Bowling average">average</a> of 26.28, playing a key role in subduing England's leading batsmen, <a href="/wiki/Len_Hutton" title="Len Hutton">Len Hutton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denis_Compton" title="Denis Compton">Denis Compton</a>, with a barrage of <a href="/wiki/Bouncer_(cricket)" title="Bouncer (cricket)">short-pitched bowling</a>. In the First Test, Miller took seven wickets, including Hutton and Compton twice, bearing a large part of the bowling workload. With the bat, he scored 184 runs in the <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Tests</a> at an <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">average</a> of 23.15, including 74 in the second <a href="/wiki/Innings" title="Innings">innings</a> of the Second Test at <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s" title="Lord's">Lord's</a>, and a rapid 58 in the Fourth Test that helped Australia regain the momentum in the match. In all <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class matches</a> on the tour, he took 56 wickets at 17.58 and scored 1,088 runs at 47.30. A carefree cricketer, Miller was seen as charismatic; his <a href="/wiki/Joie_de_vivre" title="Joie de vivre">joie de vivre</a> on the field alienated his captain, and his friendship with <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret" class="mw-redirect" title="Princess Margaret">Princess Margaret</a> was particularly scrutinised by the media. (<a href="/wiki/Keith_Miller_with_the_Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1948" title="Keith Miller with the Australian cricket team in England in 1948"><b>Full&#160;article...</b></a>)</p>
<p><i>Part of the <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Featured_topics/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1948" title="Wikipedia:Featured topics/Australian cricket team in England in 1948">Australian cricket team in England in 1948</a></b> series, one of Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Featured_topics" title="Wikipedia:Featured topics">featured topics</a>.</i></p>

<h2 id="mp-dyk-h2" style="margin:3px; background:#cef2e0; font-family:inherit; font-size:120%; font-weight:bold; border:1px solid #a3bfb1; text-align:left; color:#000; padding:0.2em 0.4em;"><span class="mw-headline" id="Did_you_know...">Did you know...</span></h2>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="color:#000; padding:2px 5px 5px;">
<div id="mp-dyk">
<div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;">
<div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 120px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schloss_Tutzing,_Blick_vom_See_zum_Haupthaus_(2).jpg" class="image" title="Schloss Tutzing"><img alt="Schloss Tutzing" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Schloss_Tutzing%2C_Blick_vom_See_zum_Haupthaus_%282%29.jpg/120px-Schloss_Tutzing%2C_Blick_vom_See_zum_Haupthaus_%282%29.jpg" width="120" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Schloss_Tutzing%2C_Blick_vom_See_zum_Haupthaus_%282%29.jpg/180px-Schloss_Tutzing%2C_Blick_vom_See_zum_Haupthaus_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Schloss_Tutzing%2C_Blick_vom_See_zum_Haupthaus_%282%29.jpg/240px-Schloss_Tutzing%2C_Blick_vom_See_zum_Haupthaus_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2693" data-file-height="2020" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">Schloss Tutzing</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>... that a speech by <a href="/wiki/Egon_Bahr" title="Egon Bahr">Egon Bahr</a> at the <b><a href="/wiki/Evangelische_Akademie_Tutzing" title="Evangelische Akademie Tutzing">Evangelische Akademie Tutzing</a></b> <i>(main building pictured)</i> influenced the <i><a href="/wiki/Ostpolitik" title="Ostpolitik">Ostpolitik</a></i> of chancellor <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a> toward the German Democratic Republic?</li>
<li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Suzuka_Mambo" title="Suzuka Mambo">Suzuka Mambo</a></b> was a Japanese racehorse sired by the American <a href="/wiki/1989_Kentucky_Derby" title="1989 Kentucky Derby">1989 Kentucky Derby</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Silence" title="Sunday Silence">Sunday Silence</a>?</li>
<li>... that <a href="/wiki/4A_Games" title="4A Games">4A Games</a> hoped that <i><b><a href="/wiki/Metro:_Last_Light" title="Metro: Last Light">Metro: Last Light</a></b></i> would "rekindle memories of <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2" title="Half-Life 2">Half-Life 2</a></i>"?</li>
<li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/South_Sudan_National_Cup" title="South Sudan National Cup">South Sudan National Cup</a></b> has been won more times by <a href="/wiki/Al-Malakia_FC" title="Al-Malakia FC">Al-Malakia FC</a> than by any other team?</li>
<li>... that since the <b><a href="/wiki/Death_and_funeral_of_Bhumibol_Adulyadej" title="Death and funeral of Bhumibol Adulyadej">death</a></b> of King <a href="/wiki/Bhumibol_Adulyadej" title="Bhumibol Adulyadej">Bhumibol Adulyadej</a>, ultra-royalists in Thailand have criticized and harassed those who did not wear mourning black?</li>
<li>... that during the <a href="/wiki/1895_Counter-revolution_in_Hawaii" title="1895 Counter-revolution in Hawaii">1895 counter-revolution</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Heleluhe" title="Joseph Heleluhe">Joseph Heleluhe</a></b>, private secretary to Hawaii's deposed queen <a href="/wiki/Liliuokalani" title="Liliuokalani">Liliuokalani</a>, was "stripped of all clothing and placed in a dark cell without light, food or water"?</li>
<li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/United_States_national_kabaddi_team" title="United States national kabaddi team">United States' team</a></b> at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Kabaddi_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 Kabaddi World Cup">2016 Kabaddi World Cup</a> consisted entirely of athletes with experience in other sports, but none in <a href="/wiki/Kabaddi" title="Kabaddi">kabaddi</a>?</li>
</ul>

<td style="padding:2px;">
<h2 id="mp-itn-h2" style="margin:3px; background:#cedff2; font-family:inherit; font-size:120%; font-weight:bold; border:1px solid #a3b0bf; text-align:left; color:#000; padding:0.2em 0.4em;"><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_news">In the news</span></h2>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="color:#000; padding:2px 5px;">
<div id="mp-itn">
<div class="itn-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;">
<div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fidel_Castro5_cropped.JPG" class="image" title="Fidel Castro in 2003"><img alt="Fidel Castro in 2003" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Fidel_Castro5_cropped.JPG/100px-Fidel_Castro5_cropped.JPG" width="100" height="139" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Fidel_Castro5_cropped.JPG/150px-Fidel_Castro5_cropped.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Fidel_Castro5_cropped.JPG/200px-Fidel_Castro5_cropped.JPG 2x" data-file-width="319" data-file-height="445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">Fidel Castro</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Former leader of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> dies at the age of 90.</li>
<li>At least 44 people are killed after <b><a href="/wiki/Semnan%E2%80%93Damghan_train_collision" title="Semnan–Damghan train collision">two passenger trains collide</a></b> between <a href="/wiki/Semnan,_Iran" title="Semnan, Iran">Semnan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Damghan" title="Damghan">Damghan</a> in Iran.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Pukhrayan_train_derailment" title="Pukhrayan train derailment">A train derailment</a></b> near <a href="/wiki/Kanpur" title="Kanpur">Kanpur</a>, India, kills more than 140 people.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Johnson" title="Jimmie Johnson">Jimmie Johnson</a> wins the <b><a href="/wiki/2016_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2016 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">NASCAR Sprint Cup Series</a></b> championship, equaling the record of seven titles held by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Petty" title="Richard Petty">Richard Petty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/2016_Kaikoura_earthquake" title="2016 Kaikoura earthquake">An earthquake</a></b> with a <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">magnitude</a> of 7.8 strikes near <a href="/wiki/Kaikoura" title="Kaikoura">Kaikoura</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a>, New Zealand, triggering tsunami warnings, causing widespread damage, and killing two people.</li>
</ul>

<h2 id="mp-otd-h2" style="margin:3px; background:#cedff2; font-family:inherit; font-size:120%; font-weight:bold; border:1px solid #a3b0bf; text-align:left; color:#000; padding:0.2em 0.4em;"><span class="mw-headline" id="On_this_day...">On this day...</span></h2>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="color:#000; padding:2px 5px 5px;">
<div id="mp-otd">
<p><b><a href="/wiki/November_28" title="November 28">November 28</a></b>: <b><a href="/wiki/Navy_Day" title="Navy Day">Navy Day</a></b> in Iran (<a href="/wiki/1980" title="1980">1980</a>)</p>
<div style="float:right;margin-left:0.5em;" id="mp-otd-img">
<div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 120px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tehran_Conference,_1943.jpg" class="image" title="Stalin, Roosevelt, and Churchill at Tehran"><img alt="Stalin, Roosevelt, and Churchill at Tehran" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Tehran_Conference%2C_1943.jpg/120px-Tehran_Conference%2C_1943.jpg" width="120" height="98" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Tehran_Conference%2C_1943.jpg/180px-Tehran_Conference%2C_1943.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Tehran_Conference%2C_1943.jpg/240px-Tehran_Conference%2C_1943.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="569" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">Stalin, Roosevelt, and Churchill at Tehran</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/936" title="936">936</a> – <b><a href="/wiki/Shi_Jingtang" title="Shi Jingtang">Shi Jingtang</a></b> was enthroned as the first emperor of the <a href="/wiki/Later_Jin_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Jin (Five Dynasties)">Later Jin</a> by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taizong_of_Liao" title="Emperor Taizong of Liao">Emperor Taizong of Liao</a>, following a revolt against <a href="/wiki/Li_Congke" title="Li Congke">Emperor Fei</a> of <a href="/wiki/Later_Tang" title="Later Tang">Later Tang</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1443" title="1443">1443</a> – Having deserted the army of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Skanderbeg" title="Skanderbeg">Skanderbeg</a></b> went to <a href="/wiki/Kruj%C3%AB" title="Krujë">Krujë</a> in Middle Albania and using a forged letter from Sultan <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Murad_II" title="Murad II">Murad II</a></span> to the Governor of Krujë, became lord of the city.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1943" title="1943">1943</a> – <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>: <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">US President</a> <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Premier of the Soviet Union">Soviet Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> <i>(all three pictured)</i> met at the <b><a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a></b> to discuss war strategy against the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1971" title="1971">1971</a> – <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Jordan" title="Prime Minister of Jordan">Prime Minister of Jordan</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Wasfi_al-Tal" title="Wasfi al-Tal">Wasfi al-Tal</a></b> was assassinated by the <a href="/wiki/Black_September_Organization" title="Black September Organization">Black September</a> unit of the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2002" title="2002">2002</a> – Suicide bombers <b><a href="/wiki/2002_Mombasa_attacks" title="2002 Mombasa attacks">blew up</a></b> an Israeli-owned hotel in <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, Kenya, but their colleagues failed in their attempt to bring down an <a href="/wiki/Arkia_Israel_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Arkia Israel Airlines">Arkia Israel Airlines</a> charter flight with surface-to-air-missiles.</li>
</ul>

<td style="padding:2px;">
<h2 id="mp-tfl-h2" style="margin:3px; background:#f2cedd; font-family:inherit; font-size:120%; font-weight:bold; border:1px solid #bfa3af; text-align:left; color:#000; padding:0.2em 0.4em"><span class="mw-headline" id="From_today.27s_featured_list">From today's featured list</span></h2>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="color:#000;">
<div id="mp-tfl" style="padding:2px 5px;">
<div id="mp-tfl-img" style="float:right;margin:0.5em 0 0.4em 0.9em;">
<div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 100px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oliver_Stone_2013.jpg" class="image" title="Oliver Stone, Best Director winner"><img alt="Oliver Stone, Best Director winner" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Oliver_Stone_2013.jpg/100px-Oliver_Stone_2013.jpg" width="100" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Oliver_Stone_2013.jpg/150px-Oliver_Stone_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Oliver_Stone_2013.jpg/200px-Oliver_Stone_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1055" data-file-height="1541" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Oliver_Stone" title="Oliver Stone">Oliver Stone</a>,</span> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Best Director</a></span> winner</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/59th_Academy_Awards" title="59th Academy Awards">59th Academy Awards</a></b> ceremony, organized by the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Motion_Picture_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences">Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences</a> (AMPAS), took place on March 30, 1987, at the <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Chandler_Pavilion" title="Dorothy Chandler Pavilion">Dorothy Chandler Pavilion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. During the ceremony, AMPAS presented <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> (commonly referred to as Oscars) in 23 categories honoring <a href="/wiki/1986_in_film" title="1986 in film">films released in 1986</a>. The ceremony, televised in the United States by <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>, was produced by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Goldwyn,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Samuel Goldwyn, Jr.">Samuel Goldwyn, Jr.</a> and directed by Marty Pasetta. Actors <a href="/wiki/Chevy_Chase" title="Chevy Chase">Chevy Chase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hogan" title="Paul Hogan">Paul Hogan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Goldie_Hawn" title="Goldie Hawn">Goldie Hawn</a> co-hosted the show. Hawn hosted the gala for the second time, having previously been a co-host of the <a href="/wiki/48th_Academy_Awards" title="48th Academy Awards">48th ceremony</a> held in 1976. Meanwhile, this was Chase and Hogan's first Oscars hosting stint. <i><a href="/wiki/Platoon_(film)" title="Platoon (film)">Platoon</a></i> won four awards including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a>. Other winners included <i><a href="/wiki/Hannah_and_Her_Sisters" title="Hannah and Her Sisters">Hannah and Her Sisters</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Room_with_a_View_(1985_film)" title="A Room with a View (1985 film)">A Room with a View</a></i> with three awards, and <i><a href="/wiki/Aliens_(film)" title="Aliens (film)">Aliens</a></i> with two awards. (<b><a href="/wiki/59th_Academy_Awards" title="59th Academy Awards">Full&#160;list...</a></b>)</p>

<h2 id="mp-tfp-h2" style="margin:3px; background:#ddcef2; font-family:inherit; font-size:120%; font-weight:bold; border:1px solid #afa3bf; text-align:left; color:#000; padding:0.2em 0.4em"><span class="mw-headline" id="Today.27s_featured_picture">Today's featured picture</span></h2>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="color:#000; padding:2px;">
<div id="mp-tfp">
<table style="margin:0 3px 3px; width:100%; text-align:left; background-color:transparent; border-collapse: collapse;">
<tr>
<td style="padding:0 0.9em 0 0;"><a href="/wiki/File:17_Years_of_Sekar_Jepun_2014-11-01_03.jpg" class="image" title="Legong Bapang Saba"><img alt="Legong Bapang Saba" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/17_Years_of_Sekar_Jepun_2014-11-01_03.jpg/300px-17_Years_of_Sekar_Jepun_2014-11-01_03.jpg" width="300" height="450" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/17_Years_of_Sekar_Jepun_2014-11-01_03.jpg/450px-17_Years_of_Sekar_Jepun_2014-11-01_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/17_Years_of_Sekar_Jepun_2014-11-01_03.jpg/600px-17_Years_of_Sekar_Jepun_2014-11-01_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2765" data-file-height="4147" /></a></td>
<td style="padding:0 6px 0 0">
<p>An adult <b><a href="/wiki/Legong" title="Legong">Legong Bapang Saba</a></b> dancer from <a href="/wiki/Sanata_Dharma_University" title="Sanata Dharma University">Sanata Dharma University</a>'s Sekar Jepun <a href="/wiki/Balinese_dance" title="Balinese dance">Balinese dance</a> troupe. Legong, which can be traced to the 19th century, is a narrative dance performed to <i><a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a></i> music. Although the fifteen types of legong have traditionally been performed by prepubescent girls, today the dance may also be performed by adult women and men in women's costumes.</p>
<p><small>Photograph: <a href="/wiki/User:Crisco_1492" title="User:Crisco 1492">Chris Woodrich</a></small></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_areas_of_Wikipedia">Other areas of Wikipedia</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Community_portal" title="Wikipedia:Community portal">Community portal</a></b> – Bulletin board, projects, resources and activities covering a wide range of Wikipedia areas.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Help_desk" title="Wikipedia:Help desk">Help desk</a></b> – Ask questions about using Wikipedia.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Local_Embassy" title="Wikipedia:Local Embassy">Local embassy</a></b> – For Wikipedia-related communication in languages other than English.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reference_desk" title="Wikipedia:Reference desk">Reference desk</a></b> – Serving as virtual librarians, Wikipedia volunteers tackle your questions on a wide range of subjects.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:News" title="Wikipedia:News">Site news</a></b> – Announcements, updates, articles and press releases on Wikipedia and the Wikimedia Foundation.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Village_pump" title="Wikipedia:Village pump">Village pump</a></b> – For discussions about Wikipedia itself, including areas for technical issues and policies.</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div id="mp-lang">
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wikipedia_languages">Wikipedia languages</span></h2>
<div id="lang" class="nowraplinks nourlexpansion plainlinks">
<p>This Wikipedia is written in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>. Started in 2001<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2001</span>)</span>, it currently contains <a href="/wiki/Special:Statistics" title="Special:Statistics">5,294,799</a> articles.  Many other Wikipedias are available; some of the largest are listed below.</p>
<ul>
<li id="lang-3">More than 1,000,000 articles:
<div class="hlist inline">
<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/"><span class="autonym" title="German (de:)" lang="de" xml:lang="de">Deutsch</span></a></li>

			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Jimmie Johnson</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">

				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div role="note" class="hatnote">This article is about the NASCAR <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a> driver. For other people named Jimmie Johnson or Jimmy Johnson, see <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Johnson_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Jimmy Johnson (disambiguation)">Jimmy Johnson (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<tr>
<th scope="row">Achievements</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/2006_NASCAR_Nextel_Cup_Series" title="2006 NASCAR Nextel Cup Series">2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_NASCAR_Nextel_Cup_Series" title="2007 NASCAR Nextel Cup Series">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2008 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2009 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2009</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2010 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2013 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2013</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2016 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2016</a> <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">NASCAR Sprint Cup Series</a> Champion<br />
Tied with <a href="/wiki/Richard_Petty" title="Richard Petty">Richard Petty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a> for most <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">NASCAR Sprint Cup Series</a> Championships (7)<br />
2003, 2006, 2012, 2013 <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Sprint_All-Star_Race" title="NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race">Sprint All-Star Race Winner</a><br />
2005 <a href="/wiki/Budweiser_Shootout" class="mw-redirect" title="Budweiser Shootout">Budweiser Shootout</a> Winner<br />
<a href="/wiki/2006_Daytona_500" title="2006 Daytona 500">2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_Daytona_500" title="2013 Daytona 500">2013 Daytona 500</a> Winner<br />
2003, 2004, 2005, <a href="/wiki/2014_Coca-Cola_600" title="2014 Coca-Cola 600">2014 Coca-Cola 600</a> Winner<br />
2006, <a href="/wiki/2008_Brickyard_400" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Brickyard 400">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_Allstate_400_at_the_Brickyard" title="2009 Allstate 400 at the Brickyard">2009</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Brickyard_400" title="2012 Brickyard 400">2012 Brickyard 400</a> Winner<br />
2004, 2012 <a href="/wiki/Southern_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern 500">Southern 500</a> Winner<br />
10 wins at <a href="/wiki/Dover_International_Speedway" title="Dover International Speedway">Dover International Speedway</a> (including 2 sweeps in 2002 and 2009)<br />
Nine wins at <a href="/wiki/Martinsville_Speedway" title="Martinsville Speedway">Martinsville Speedway</a> (including a sweep in 2007, and 2006–2008, 2012, 2016 Chase race wins)<br />
2010 <a href="/wiki/Prelude_to_the_Dream" title="Prelude to the Dream">Prelude to the Dream</a> Winner<br />
Six off-road racing championships</td>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><i>Statistics current as of November 20, 2016.</i></td>

<p><b>Jimmie Kenneth Johnson</b> (born September 17, 1975) is an American <a href="/wiki/Stock_car_racing" title="Stock car racing">stock car racing</a> driver and a seven-time champion in the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a>. He currently drives the No. 48 <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_SS_(2013)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet SS (2013)">Chevrolet SS</a> for <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Motorsports" title="Hendrick Motorsports">Hendrick Motorsports</a>.</p>
<p>Johnson was born in <a href="/wiki/El_Cajon,_California" title="El Cajon, California">El Cajon, California</a>, and began racing motorcycles at the age of four. After graduating from <a href="/wiki/Granite_Hills_High_School_(El_Cajon,_California)" title="Granite Hills High School (El Cajon, California)">Granite Hills High School</a> he competed in <a href="/wiki/Off-road_racing" title="Off-road racing">off-road</a> series. He raced in <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Thompson_Entertainment_Group" title="Mickey Thompson Entertainment Group">Mickey Thompson Entertainment Group</a> (MTEG), <a href="/wiki/Short-course_Off-road_Drivers_Association" title="Short-course Off-road Drivers Association">Short-course Off-road Drivers Association</a> (SODA) and <a href="/wiki/SCORE_International" title="SCORE International">SCORE International</a>, winning rookie of the year in each series. In 1998, Johnson and his team, <a href="/wiki/Herzog_Motorsports" class="mw-redirect" title="Herzog Motorsports">Herzog Motorsports</a>, began stock car racing. He moved to the national <a href="/wiki/American_Speed_Association" title="American Speed Association">American Speed Association</a> (ASA) series for <a href="/wiki/Late_model" title="Late model">late model</a> touring cars, and won another rookie of the year title. In 2000, he switched to the NASCAR Busch Series (now <a href="/wiki/Xfinity_Series" title="Xfinity Series">Xfinity Series</a>).</p>
<p>He moved to Hendrick Motorsports in the Sprint Cup Series in 2002. After finishing fifth in the points in his first full season, he was second in 2003 and 2004 and fifth in 2005. Johnson won his first Cup Series championship in 2006 and with further wins in 2007, 2008, 2009, and 2010, he became the first and only driver in NASCAR history to win five consecutive championships. Johnson finished sixth in the points standings in the 2011 season and third in 2012 before winning his sixth championship in 2013. In 2016, Johnson won his seventh championship, tying <a href="/wiki/Richard_Petty" title="Richard Petty">Richard Petty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a> for the most Cup Series championships of all time. Johnson is also a two-time winner of the <a href="/wiki/Daytona_500" title="Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a>, winning in <a href="/wiki/2006_Daytona_500" title="2006 Daytona 500">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_Daytona_500" title="2013 Daytona 500">2013</a>. Between 2002 and 2016, Johnson has recorded seven championships, 80 career race wins, 219 top fives, 330 top tens, and 35 <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole positions</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Racing_career">Racing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Racing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings">Beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Johnson started racing motorcycles in 1980 when he was four. Three years later, he won the 60cc class championship, despite having an injured knee.<sup id="cite_ref-hendrickbiography_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hendrickbiography-1">[1]</a></sup> Afterward, he moved to the <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Thompson_Entertainment_Group" title="Mickey Thompson Entertainment Group">Mickey Thompson Entertainment Group</a> (MTEG) Stadium Racing Series where he won several more awards. In 1993, Johnson was given the opportunity to drive for Herb Fishel. He refused the deal and continued racing <a href="/wiki/Baja_Bug" title="Baja Bug">buggies</a> and trucks in off-road stadium and desert races. He also reported for <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> in the <a href="/wiki/SCORE_International" title="SCORE International">Short Course Off-Road Drivers Association</a> (SODA). Three years later, Johnson drove for <a href="/wiki/Herzog-Jackson_Motorsports" class="mw-redirect" title="Herzog-Jackson Motorsports">Herzog Motorsports</a> in the off-road truck series in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-hendrickbiography_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hendrickbiography-1">[1]</a></sup> By 1997, Johnson had progressed to SODA's Class 8; Class 8 is short-course off-road racing's class of two-wheel-drive <a href="/wiki/Trophy_Truck" title="Trophy Truck">Trophy Trucks</a> which generate about 800 horsepower.<sup id="cite_ref-Motorsport1997_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motorsport1997-2">[2]</a></sup> He battled <a href="/wiki/Scott_Taylor_(racing_driver)" title="Scott Taylor (racing driver)">Scott Taylor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Gaughan" title="Brendan Gaughan">Brendan Gaughan</a> for the championship.<sup id="cite_ref-Motorsport1997_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motorsport1997-2">[2]</a></sup> That year, Johnson won both races at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva_Raceway" title="Lake Geneva Raceway">Lake Geneva Raceway</a>'s first race weekend in May.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> He also won the season's third event at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Langlade_County_Fairgrounds&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Langlade County Fairgrounds (page does not exist)">Antigo</a> before finishing second to Gaughan at Antigo's second race.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Johnson returned to Lake Geneva in July, winning the Saturday race and finished 2nd on the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Taylor ended up winning the championship with Gaughan second and Johnson third.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> During his time in the SODA, SCORE and MTEG series, he accumulated over 25 wins, 100 top-three finishes, six championships, and received Rookie of the Year honors in all three leagues.<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiejohnsonorg_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiejohnsonorg-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998, he began racing on asphalt <a href="/wiki/Oval_track_racing" title="Oval track racing">ovals</a> when he entered the <a href="/wiki/American_Speed_Association" title="American Speed Association">American Speed Association</a> (ASA)<sup id="cite_ref-Speed51_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Speed51-8">[8]</a></sup> as well as part-time in the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> Busch Series (now <a href="/wiki/Xfinity_Series" title="Xfinity Series">Xfinity Series</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-hendrickbiography_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hendrickbiography-1">[1]</a></sup> In the same year, Johnson won the ASA Pat Schauer Memorial Rookie title.<sup id="cite_ref-Speed51_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Speed51-8">[8]</a></sup> One year later, he had two wins and finished third in the standings.<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiejohnsonorg_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiejohnsonorg-7">[7]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2000_NASCAR_Busch_Series" title="2000 NASCAR Busch Series">2000</a>, he was announced the driver for Herzog Motorsports in the Busch Series. During the season, he had a spectacular accident on lap 46 during the Lysol 200 at Watkins Glen when his brakes failed entering the first turn. He had to swerve quickly to the right to avoid the 86 of Dennis Demers, but went into the grass on the inside of turn one, then went back across the track, caught some air on the gravel trap before finally crashing head-on into the carafoam barriers at the far end of the turn while still more than 150+ MPH. Many feared that this accident could have resulted in career ending injuries or potentially have killed him, but he climbed out of the car unscathed and raised his fists in the air like he'd won the race, much to the delight of the crowd. Otherwise, in a rather uneventful season which featured one DNQ at Daytona and 6 top-10's, he finished tenth in the point standings. During the <a href="/wiki/2001_NASCAR_Busch_Series" title="2001 NASCAR Busch Series">2001 season</a>, Johnson recorded one win, which was at <a href="/wiki/Chicagoland_Speedway" title="Chicagoland Speedway">Chicagoland Speedway</a>, and finished eighth in the point standings. He also began racing in the Winston Cup Series (now <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a>) for <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Motorsports" title="Hendrick Motorsports">Hendrick Motorsports</a>. In the following season, Johnson left Herzog Motorsports to move to Hendrick Motorsports in the Winston Cup Series, driving the No. 48 <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">Lowe's</a> Chevrolet.<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiejohnsonorg_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiejohnsonorg-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sprint_Cup_Series">Sprint Cup Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Sprint Cup Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.9305">2002–05</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2002–05">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Johnson began racing full-time in the Winston Cup Series during the <a href="/wiki/2002_NASCAR_Winston_Cup_Series" title="2002 NASCAR Winston Cup Series">2002 season</a>. He earned his first career <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole position</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2002_Daytona_500" title="2002 Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a>, becoming the second rookie to do so (the first was <a href="/wiki/Loy_Allen,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Loy Allen, Jr.">Loy Allen, Jr.</a> in <a href="/wiki/1994_Daytona_500" title="1994 Daytona 500">1994</a>). In his 13th career start, Johnson scored his first career win in the NAPA Auto Parts 500 at <a href="/wiki/Auto_Club_Speedway" title="Auto Club Speedway">Auto Club Speedway</a>. Johnson became the first rookie driver to lead the point standings and to win twice at the same track during a season, by sweeping both races at <a href="/wiki/Dover_International_Speedway" title="Dover International Speedway">Dover</a>. He recorded four pole positions and three wins (tying the rookie record set by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Stewart" title="Tony Stewart">Tony Stewart</a> in 1999),<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> as well as six top fives and twenty-one top ten finishes. He finished fifth in the final point standings.<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiejohnsonorg_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiejohnsonorg-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/2003_NASCAR_Winston_Cup_Series" title="2003 NASCAR Winston Cup Series">2003</a>, Johnson finished ninth on the all-time list for consecutive weeks ranked in the top ten in points with 69. He won three races (Coca-Cola 600 at Charlotte and both New Hampshire races), two poles (at <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Speedway" title="Kansas Speedway">Kansas Speedway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pocono_Raceway" title="Pocono Raceway">Pocono Raceway</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup> fourteen top fives, and twenty top ten finishes. He also was able to win the All-Star race for the first time, as well as finishing second with just 90 points behind <a href="/wiki/Matt_Kenseth" title="Matt Kenseth">Matt Kenseth</a> and 207 ahead of his future teammate <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JimmieJohnsonCalifornia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/JimmieJohnsonCalifornia.jpg/200px-JimmieJohnsonCalifornia.jpg" width="200" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/JimmieJohnsonCalifornia.jpg/300px-JimmieJohnsonCalifornia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/98/JimmieJohnsonCalifornia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="220" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JimmieJohnsonCalifornia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson qualifying at <a href="/wiki/Auto_Club_Speedway" title="Auto Club Speedway">Auto Club Speedway</a> in 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2004_NASCAR_Nextel_Cup_Series" title="2004 NASCAR Nextel Cup Series">2004</a>, Johnson started slowly at <a href="/wiki/Rockingham_Speedway" title="Rockingham Speedway">Rockingham Speedway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Motor_Speedway" title="Las Vegas Motor Speedway">Las Vegas Motor Speedway</a> with results of 41st and 16th, after a top ten finish in the Daytona 500. However, he quickly was able to rebound winning the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Dodge_Dealers_400" title="Carolina Dodge Dealers 400">Carolina Dodge Dealers 400</a> at <a href="/wiki/Darlington_Raceway" title="Darlington Raceway">Darlington Raceway</a>. Subsequent victories in the <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_600" title="Coca-Cola 600">Coca-Cola 600</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pocono_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Pocono 500">Pocono 500</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Pennsylvania 500">Pennsylvania 500</a> came in the middle of the season, seeing Johnson sweep the Pocono races. However, finishes of 37th and 32nd at <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a> and Kansas moved him toward the bottom of the point standings. Afterward, he was able to win the <a href="/wiki/UAW-GM_Quality_500" class="mw-redirect" title="UAW-GM Quality 500">UAW-GM Quality 500</a> at Lowe's Motor Speedway. The second victory of the 2004 Chase for the Nextel Cup, at the <a href="/wiki/2004_Subway_500" title="2004 Subway 500">Subway 500</a> at Martinsville on October 24, 2004, was marred by tragedy. Owner <a href="/wiki/Rick_Hendrick" title="Rick Hendrick">Rick Hendrick</a>'s son <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Hendrick" title="Ricky Hendrick">Ricky</a>, twin nieces, brother, and chief engine builder <a href="/wiki/Randy_Dorton" title="Randy Dorton">Randy Dorton</a> as well as Joe Turner, Scott Lathram were killed in an airplane crash en route to the race. All eight passengers and both pilots died in the incident, and Johnson was told after completion of the race.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Johnson had a total of eight wins, 20 top five and 23 top ten finishes. At the end of the season, Johnson finished second in the point standings.<sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stats2004_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats2004-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, Johnson won at <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Motor_Speedway" title="Las Vegas Motor Speedway">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s_Motor_Speedway" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowe's Motor Speedway">Lowe's Motor Speedway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dover_International_Speedway" title="Dover International Speedway">Dover International Speedway</a>, and then again at Lowe's. In total, Johnson had four consecutive wins at his sponsor (<a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">Lowe's</a>) sponsored track in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a>. Johnson had a chance to win the championship coming into the November 20 season finale at <a href="/wiki/Homestead-Miami_Speedway" title="Homestead-Miami Speedway">Homestead-Miami Speedway</a>, but finished 5th in points after crashing at the midway point of the event with a tire problem.<sup id="cite_ref-stats2005_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats2005-15">[15]</a></sup> He scored 13 top-fives, 22 top-10 finishes, and one pole position.<sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2006.E2.80.932010:_Championship_streak">2006–2010: Championship streak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2006–2010: Championship streak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2006">2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2006_NASCAR_Nextel_Cup_Series" title="2006 NASCAR Nextel Cup Series">2006</a>, Johnson began the season by winning the <a href="/wiki/2006_Daytona_500" title="2006 Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a>. He finished second in the next race at <a href="/wiki/Auto_Club_Speedway" title="Auto Club Speedway">California Speedway</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/UAW-Dodge_400" class="mw-redirect" title="UAW-Dodge 400">UAW-DaimlerChrysler 400</a> at <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Motor_Speedway" title="Las Vegas Motor Speedway">Las Vegas</a>. Johnson won his third race of the season in the <a href="/wiki/Brickyard_400" title="Brickyard 400">Brickyard 400</a> followed by two more victories at Martinsville and Talladega. Throughout the season, he became the only modern era driver to win at least three races in each of his first five seasons. At the end of the season, he recorded one pole, 13 top fives, 24 top tens, and his first championship title (this was also the first in his NASCAR career). In December, Johnson won 2006 <a href="/wiki/Driver_of_the_Year" title="Driver of the Year">Driver of the Year</a> Award.<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiejohnsonorg_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiejohnsonorg-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stats2006_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats2006-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2007_NASCAR_Nextel_Cup_Series" title="2007 NASCAR Nextel Cup Series">2007 season</a>, Johnson continued on a streak and recorded 10 wins, four poles, 20 top fives, and again 24 top ten finishes. Those 10 wins included sweeping both races at Richmond, Atlanta, and Martinsville. He also won at Las Vegas,<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiejohnsonorg_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiejohnsonorg-7">[7]</a></sup> Auto Club, Texas, and Phoenix. Afterwards, he won his second consecutive championship title and was named the 2007 Driver of the Year. Johnson also had the best average finish in the Chase with 5.0. At the end of the season, he had a total of 33 career wins, placing him 18th on the all-time wins list.<sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stats2007_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats2007-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2007, Johnson commenced a program of exercise sessions and a run schedule supervised by <a href="/wiki/John_Sitaras" title="John Sitaras">John Sitaras</a>, in order to balance his strength. Sitaras' initial assessment found that half of his body was much tighter, having acclimated to offsetting the <a href="/wiki/G-force" title="G-force">g-force</a> load from turning left while driving.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In two years, Johnson's body fat percentage dropped from 20% to 8% (visible also in the change of the shape of his face), while his strength and stamina greatly improved.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-20">[20]</a></sup> Johnson later became the first racing driver to be named <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press_Male_Athlete_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Associated Press Male Athlete of the Year">Associated Press Male Athlete of the Year</a> (in 2009).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2008">2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg/200px-Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg/300px-Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg/400px-Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1664" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_2008_Lowes_Chevy_Impala.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jimmie Johnson racing in the <a href="/wiki/2008_Daytona_500" title="2008 Daytona 500">2008 Daytona 500</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/2008_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2008 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2008 season</a>, Johnson became the second driver to win three consecutive Sprint Cup Series championships, the first being <a href="/wiki/Cale_Yarborough" title="Cale Yarborough">Cale Yarborough</a>. During the season, he managed to win seven races (including a sweep at <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_International_Raceway" title="Phoenix International Raceway">Phoenix</a>), a career high of six poles, 15 top fives, and 22 top tens. In five of those seven wins, he started from the pole. He became the only driver to record three wins in each of their first seven seasons. In the Chase for the Sprint Cup, he recorded 14 wins, eight more than any other driver. He also was named the 2008 Driver of the Year and won an <a href="/wiki/ESPY" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPY">ESPY</a> as the Best Driver. After the season, he also moved to third on the active winners list.<sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stats2008_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats2008-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2009">2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2009_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2009 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2009 season</a>, Johnson recorded his fourth consecutive championship, becoming the only driver to win four back-to-back season titles. Throughout this season, he won seven races (including a third consecutive <a href="/wiki/Quicken_Loans_Race_for_Heroes_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Quicken Loans Race for Heroes 500">Checker Auto Parts 500</a> and both Dover races), four poles, 16 top fives, and 24 top ten finishes. Johnson now became the only driver to win at least three races in each of his first eight seasons, as well as the only driver to qualify for the Chase for the Sprint Cup every year since 2004. During the season, he moved up one spot up to second on the active winners list and went to 13th on the all-time wins list. After the season concluded, he won an ESPY for the second consecutive year, and won the Driver of the Year award for the third time, tying <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Andretti" title="Mario Andretti">Mario Andretti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Waltrip" title="Darrell Waltrip">Darrell Waltrip</a> as the only three time drivers to win the award.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/2010_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2010 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2010</a>, Johnson managed to win his fifth consecutive championship, becoming the third driver who made up points to win the title since 1975. During the season, he scored two poles, 17 top fives, 23 top tens and six victories. He also remained the only driver to qualify for the Chase every year since its inception in 2004 and went up to 10th on the all time wins list. Johnson was also named Driver of the Year for the fourth time in his career, joining Gordon as the only drivers to win the award that many times.<sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> He also managed to win <a href="/wiki/Tony_Stewart" title="Tony Stewart">Tony Stewart</a>'s charity race, the <a href="/wiki/Prelude_to_the_Dream" title="Prelude to the Dream">Prelude to the Dream</a>, his first victory on a dirt oval.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg/220px-JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg/330px-JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg/440px-JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JG_24_and_JJ_48_-_Charlotte_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson (No. 5) and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2011_NASCAR_Sprint_All-Star_Race" title="2011 NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race">2011 All-Star Race</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2011_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2011 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2011</a>, Johnson began the season with a fourth place finish in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Budweiser_Shootout" title="2011 Budweiser Shootout">Budweiser Shootout</a>, after starting from the 23rd position.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> One week later in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Daytona_500" title="2011 Daytona 500">2011 Daytona 500</a>, he started 23rd, but finished 27th after being involved in a <a href="/wiki/The_Big_One_(NASCAR)" title="The Big One (NASCAR)">crash</a> on lap 29.<sup id="cite_ref-trevorbaynewinsdaytona_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trevorbaynewinsdaytona-29">[29]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2011_Subway_Fresh_Fit_500" title="2011 Subway Fresh Fit 500">Subway Fresh Fit 500</a>, he managed a third place finish. Following a 16th place finish after the <a href="/wiki/2011_Kobalt_Tools_400" title="2011 Kobalt Tools 400">Kobalt Tools 400</a> he collected two consecutive top-five finishes.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Statistically, Johnson's 2011 season was his second worst performance to date, even though he finished sixth in the points. He only won two races during the season. The first was the <a href="/wiki/2011_Aaron%27s_499" title="2011 Aaron's 499">Aaron's 499</a> at <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a>, where Johnson started on the outside pole, and tandem-drafted with <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a> for the entire race. On the last lap, with Johnson in front, he and Earnhardt, Jr. were in fifth and sixth off of turn 4, behind two other pairs of cars - their Hendrick teammates <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Martin" title="Mark Martin">Mark Martin</a>, and the Richard Childress drafting pair of <a href="/wiki/Clint_Bowyer" title="Clint Bowyer">Clint Bowyer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Harvick" title="Kevin Harvick">Kevin Harvick</a>. In the tri-oval, Earnhardt, Jr. gave Johnson enough of a push to nip Bowyer at the finish line by 0.002 seconds. This was the closest recorded finish in Talladega history, and tied the <a href="/wiki/2003_Carolina_Dodge_Dealers_400" title="2003 Carolina Dodge Dealers 400">2003 Carolina Dodge Dealers 400</a> for closest margin of victory in NASCAR history.<sup id="cite_ref-talladegaclose_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talladegaclose-30">[30]</a></sup> After finishing in the first 15 positions in the next four races, Johnson failed to finish the <a href="/wiki/2011_Coca-Cola_600" title="2011 Coca-Cola 600">Coca-Cola 600</a> after his engine failed.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> The next week, in the <a href="/wiki/Heluva_Good!_Sour_Cream_Dips_400" class="mw-redirect" title="Heluva Good! Sour Cream Dips 400">Heluva Good! Sour Cream Dips 400</a>, Johnson spun off turn two, flattening multiple tires, and breaking the <a href="/wiki/Sway_bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Sway bar">sway bar</a> which prompted him to a finish of 27th.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2011_Toyota/Save_Mart_350" title="2011 Toyota/Save Mart 350">Toyota/Save Mart 350</a>, Johnson finished seventh after starting 12th on the grid. The finish moved Johnson to third in the Drivers' standings.<sup id="cite_ref-hendrickinfineon_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hendrickinfineon-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>After returning to <a href="/wiki/Daytona_International_Speedway" title="Daytona International Speedway">Daytona International Speedway</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Coke_Zero_400" title="2011 Coke Zero 400">Coke Zero 400</a>, Johnson and Earnhardt, Jr. ran together for most of the race, like at Talladega, until Johnson pitted under a caution flag. Johnson fell down the grid and was involved in a last lap accident, prompting him to finish 20th.<sup id="cite_ref-johnsonearnhardt_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnsonearnhardt-33">[33]</a></sup> During the next two races, Johnson finished third and fifth in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Quaker_State_400" title="2011 Quaker State 400">Quaker State 400</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2011_Lenox_Industrial_Tools_301" title="2011 Lenox Industrial Tools 301">Lenox Industrial Tools 301</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> Two weeks later, Johnson found himself finishing 19th during the <a href="/wiki/2011_Brickyard_400" title="2011 Brickyard 400">Brickyard 400</a> after coming to pit road with 30 laps remaining in the event.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Johnson finished fourth in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Good_Sam_RV_Insurance_500" title="2011 Good Sam RV Insurance 500">Good Sam RV Insurance 500</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> after bumping <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Busch" title="Kurt Busch">Kurt Busch</a> on the final lap.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In the next <a href="/wiki/Heluva_Good!_Sour_Cream_Dips_at_the_Glen" class="mw-redirect" title="Heluva Good! Sour Cream Dips at the Glen">race</a>, Johnson managed to finish tenth.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> Johnson finished in the top-five in the following three races.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> During the last race of the regular season, the <a href="/wiki/Wonderful_Pistachios_400" class="mw-redirect" title="Wonderful Pistachios 400">Wonderful Pistachios 400</a>, Johnson finished in the 31st position.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> While at <a href="/wiki/Chicagoland_Speedway" title="Chicagoland Speedway">Chicagoland Speedway</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2011_GEICO_400" title="2011 GEICO 400">GEICO 400</a>, Johnson finished 10th.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> Afterward, Johnson managed to finish 18th in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Sylvania_300" title="2011 Sylvania 300">Sylvania 300</a>, then second in the <a href="/wiki/2011_AAA_400" title="2011 AAA 400">AAA 400</a>. One week later, Johnson recorded his second victory of the season in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Hollywood_Casino_400" title="2011 Hollywood Casino 400">Hollywood Casino 400</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2011_Bank_of_America_500" title="2011 Bank of America 500">Bank of America 500</a>, Johnson was involved in a crash and finished 34th. In the following <a href="/wiki/2011_Tums_Fast_Relief_500" title="2011 Tums Fast Relief 500">race</a>, Johnson finished second. For the next two races, Johnson finished 14th in each, and finished 32nd in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Ford_400" title="2011 Ford 400">Ford 400</a> to finish sixth in the Driver's championship standings.<sup id="cite_ref-2011season_28-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011season-28">[28]</a></sup> The Championship, for the first time since 2006, went to Tony Stewart.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2012">2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Johnson began the <a href="/wiki/2012_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2012 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2012 season</a> with a 14th place finish in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Budweiser_Shootout" title="2012 Budweiser Shootout">Budweiser Shootout</a> after crashing on lap 74.<sup id="cite_ref-2012budshootout_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012budshootout-36">[36]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2012_Daytona_500" title="2012 Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a>, Johnson was involved in a crash on lap 2 when he turned into the wall after contact from <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Sadler" title="Elliott Sadler">Elliott Sadler</a>, then was t-boned by <a href="/wiki/David_Ragan" title="David Ragan">David Ragan</a>, also collecting <a href="/wiki/Danica_Patrick" title="Danica Patrick">Danica Patrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Busch" title="Kurt Busch">Kurt Busch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Bayne" title="Trevor Bayne">Trevor Bayne</a>. Damage to the car was severe, prompting him to retire and finish 42nd.<sup id="cite_ref-johnson2012daytona500wreck_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnson2012daytona500wreck-37">[37]</a></sup> Afterward, he finished fourth and second in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Subway_Fresh_Fit_500" title="2012 Subway Fresh Fit 500">Subway Fresh Fit 500</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_Kobalt_Tools_400" title="2012 Kobalt Tools 400">Kobalt Tools 400</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2012season_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012season-38">[38]</a></sup> While at Bristol Motor Speedway for the <a href="/wiki/Food_City_500" title="Food City 500">Food City 500</a>, Johnson finished in the ninth position, moving him up to 11th<sup id="cite_ref-addmorepoints_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-addmorepoints-39">[39]</a></sup> in the Drivers' Standings.<sup id="cite_ref-bristolhendrick9th_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bristolhendrick9th-40">[40]</a></sup> Next, Johnson finished tenth in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Auto_Club_400" title="2012 Auto Club 400">Auto Club 400</a>, despite having an oil leak,<sup id="cite_ref-oiltenth_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oiltenth-41">[41]</a></sup> but the rain saved Johnson from a low finish. He went on to finish twelfth during the <a href="/wiki/2012_Goody%27s_Fast_Relief_500" title="2012 Goody's Fast Relief 500">spring event</a> at <a href="/wiki/Martinsville_Speedway" title="Martinsville Speedway">Martinsville</a> after being involved in a crash on the first <a href="/wiki/Green-white-checker" class="mw-redirect" title="Green-white-checker">green-white-checker</a> attempt.<sup id="cite_ref-Martinsvillespring12finish_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martinsvillespring12finish-42">[42]</a></sup> In the following event, the <a href="/wiki/2012_Samsung_Mobile_500" title="2012 Samsung Mobile 500">Samsung Mobile 500</a>, Johnson finished second after leading much of the race before he was passed by <a href="/wiki/Greg_Biffle" title="Greg Biffle">Greg Biffle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-texasbiffle2nd_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-texasbiffle2nd-43">[43]</a></sup> Afterward, he recorded a third place finish in the <a href="/wiki/2012_STP_400" title="2012 STP 400">STP 400</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Speedway" title="Kansas Speedway">Kansas</a> on April 22, 2012, and a sixth place finish in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Capital_City_400" title="2012 Capital City 400">Capital City 400</a> at <a href="/wiki/Richmond_International_Raceway" title="Richmond International Raceway">Richmond</a> one week later.<sup id="cite_ref-2012season_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012season-38">[38]</a></sup> On May 6, 2012, Johnson started 19th in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Aaron%27s_499" title="2012 Aaron's 499">Aaron's 499</a> at <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega</a>, but finished 35th after his engine failed on lap 110.<sup id="cite_ref-lapbylaptalladegaspring_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lapbylaptalladegaspring-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg/200px-Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg/300px-Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg/400px-Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2233" data-file-height="1485" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_on_pit_road.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson pits his car in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Johnson won his first race of the season one week later in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Bojangles%27_Southern_500" title="2012 Bojangles' Southern 500">Bojangles' Southern 500</a> at <a href="/wiki/Darlington_Raceway" title="Darlington Raceway">Darlington</a>. The win was also <a href="/wiki/Rick_Hendrick" title="Rick Hendrick">Rick Hendrick</a>'s 200th Sprint Cup Series win.<sup id="cite_ref-200finally_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200finally-45">[45]</a></sup> A week later, he matched Gordon and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a> with three wins in the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Sprint_All-Star_Race" title="NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race">NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race</a> after winning the <a href="/wiki/2012_NASCAR_Sprint_All-Star_Race" title="2012 NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race">2012 NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jjwinallstar_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jjwinallstar-46">[46]</a></sup> Next, in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Coca-Cola_600" title="2012 Coca-Cola 600">Coca-Cola 600</a>, Johnson finished 11th in the race after a penalty on lap 354.<sup id="cite_ref-11incharlotte2012_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11incharlotte2012-47">[47]</a></sup> After the Coca-Cola 600, Johnson went on to win his second race of the season in the <a href="/wiki/2012_FedEx_400" title="2012 FedEx 400">FedEx 400</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiewinsdoverseven_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiewinsdoverseven-48">[48]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2012_Pocono_400" title="2012 Pocono 400">Pocono 400</a>, he recorded a fourth place finish after starting 24th on the grid.<sup id="cite_ref-johnsonralliesforfourth_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnsonralliesforfourth-49">[49]</a></sup> During the next two races, Johnson placed fifth,<sup id="cite_ref-2012season_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012season-38">[38]</a></sup> moving him to fourth in the standings.<sup id="cite_ref-topofiveatsonoma_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-topofiveatsonoma-50">[50]</a></sup> Afterward, Johnson finished sixth after winning his first pole position of the season in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Quaker_State_400" title="2012 Quaker State 400">Quaker State 400</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kentuckyfinish2012_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kentuckyfinish2012-51">[51]</a></sup> However, in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Coke_Zero_400" title="2012 Coke Zero 400">Coke Zero 400</a>, Johnson finished 36th<sup id="cite_ref-2012season_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012season-38">[38]</a></sup> after retiring from a crash on lap 124.<sup id="cite_ref-wreckincokezero4002012_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wreckincokezero4002012-52">[52]</a></sup> After finishing seventh during the <a href="/wiki/2012_Lenox_Industrial_Tools_301" title="2012 Lenox Industrial Tools 301">Lenox Industrial Tools 301</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2012season_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012season-38">[38]</a></sup> Johnson recorded his third victory of the season and his fourth career win at the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Motor_Speedway" title="Indianapolis Motor Speedway">Indianapolis Motor Speedway</a>, tying <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a> for what was the record for the most wins in the <a href="/wiki/Brickyard_400" title="Brickyard 400">Brickyard 400</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-johnsonwinsbrickyard4_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnsonwinsbrickyard4-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>After making the <a href="/wiki/Chase_for_the_Sprint_Cup" title="Chase for the Sprint Cup">Chase for the Sprint Cup</a>, Johnson secured three straight top five finishes in the <a href="/wiki/2012_GEICO_400" title="2012 GEICO 400">GEICO 400</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Sylvania_300" title="2012 Sylvania 300">Sylvania 300</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_AAA_400" title="2012 AAA 400">AAA 400</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2012season_38-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012season-38">[38]</a></sup> Following a seventeenth place finish in <a href="/wiki/2012_Good_Sam_Roadside_Assistance_500" title="2012 Good Sam Roadside Assistance 500">Good Sam Roadside Assistance 500</a>, Johnson recorded four top-ten finishes,<sup id="cite_ref-2012season_38-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012season-38">[38]</a></sup> including two consecutive wins from the pole position at <a href="/wiki/2012_Tums_Fast_Relief_500" title="2012 Tums Fast Relief 500">Martinsville</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_AAA_Texas_500" title="2012 AAA Texas 500">Texas</a>, which was his sixtieth win in the series, to take a seven-point lead over <a href="/wiki/Brad_Keselowski" title="Brad Keselowski">Brad Keselowski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-johnsonmartinsvilletexas2012_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnsonmartinsvilletexas2012-54">[54]</a></sup> At Phoenix, Johnson blew a right front tire, which caused him to collide into the wall and finish in the 32nd position.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> He was racing for the win and the championship the following week at Homestead, but his chances of winning the championship was over after he had a pit road penalty and had a gear failure and he finished 36th in that race, and finished third in the Drivers Championship behind Keselowski and Bowyer.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013:_Return_to_championship_form">2013: Return to championship form</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2013: Return to championship form">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson,_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Jimmie_Johnson%2C_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg/220px-Jimmie_Johnson%2C_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Jimmie_Johnson%2C_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg/330px-Jimmie_Johnson%2C_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Jimmie_Johnson%2C_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg/440px-Jimmie_Johnson%2C_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2406" data-file-height="1805" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson,_2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson racing during the <a href="/wiki/2013_STP_Gas_Booster_500" title="2013 STP Gas Booster 500">2013 STP Gas Booster 500</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg/220px-Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg/330px-Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg/440px-Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1057" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_Hendrick_Motorsports_Texas_April_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson during practice for the <a href="/wiki/2013_NRA_500" title="2013 NRA 500">2013 NRA 500</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2013_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2013 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2013</a>, Johnson began his season with a 14th-place finish in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Sprint_Unlimited" title="2013 Sprint Unlimited">2013 Sprint Unlimited</a> when he crashed on lap 14 along with <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Busch" title="Kyle Busch">Kyle Busch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Busch" title="Kurt Busch">Kurt Busch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Martin" title="Mark Martin">Mark Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hamlin" title="Denny Hamlin">Denny Hamlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2013season_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013season-57">[57]</a></sup> Afterward, he placed fourth in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Budweiser_Duels" title="2013 Budweiser Duels">first Budweiser Duel</a>, resulting in a ninth-place starting position in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Daytona_500" title="2013 Daytona 500">2013 Daytona 500</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2013season_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013season-57">[57]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2013_Daytona_500" title="2013 Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a>, Johnson started well, assuming the lead from <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a> on lap 33 and leading a handful of laps before falling back to the middle of the pack. Over the last few laps, Johnson was racing alongside <a href="/wiki/Brad_Keselowski" title="Brad Keselowski">Brad Keselowski</a> for the lead until a caution came out for debris. Johnson took the advantage of leading on the last restart. With five laps to go, Johnson led a lane with <a href="/wiki/Greg_Biffle" title="Greg Biffle">Greg Biffle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danica_Patrick" title="Danica Patrick">Danica Patrick</a>. He then held off a last lap charge from <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Martin" title="Mark Martin">Mark Martin</a> to win his second Daytona 500.<sup id="cite_ref-daytonawin2013_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daytonawin2013-58">[58]</a></sup> This was Johnson's first Daytona 500 win with regular crew chief Chad Knaus, as he won the 2006 race with <a href="/wiki/Darian_Grubb" title="Darian Grubb">Darian Grubb</a> as Knaus was serving a five-race suspension. It was also the first time since his 2006 win that he finished better than 27th in the Daytona 500, after a streak of six years where he had never finished better than 27th because of crashes and mechanical failures.</p>
<p>The following week at Phoenix, Johnson started inside the top ten and finished second behind <a href="/wiki/Carl_Edwards" title="Carl Edwards">Carl Edwards</a>. He followed this with a sixth-place finish at Las Vegas. At Bristol, he was running on the lead lap until a spin late race forced him back to a 22nd-place finish. At Fontana, he struggled for most of the race, racing near the back of the pack, but managed to salvage a 12th-place finish. Johnson won his first pole position of the season at Martinsville and had the dominant car, leading 346 of 500 laps on the way to his eighth Martinsville race win. Johnson also assumed the point lead as well, which he would hold on to for the remainder of the regular season.
