Johnson's consistency was enough that there were points in the summer where he was more than a full two race wins' worth of points ahead of <a href="/wiki/Carl_Edwards" title="Carl Edwards">Carl Edwards</a> or <a href="/wiki/Clint_Bowyer" title="Clint Bowyer">Clint Bowyer</a>. Afterward, Johnson finished sixth at Texas. At Kansas, he led nine laps and finished third behind <a href="/wiki/Matt_Kenseth" title="Matt Kenseth">Matt Kenseth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kasey_Kahne" title="Kasey Kahne">Kasey Kahne</a>. Johnson finished 12th the following week at Richmond, allowing him to build even further on his point lead. At Talladega, he was the only driver besides <a href="/wiki/Matt_Kenseth" title="Matt Kenseth">Matt Kenseth</a> to lead double digit laps (16), and finished in fifth place. A fourth-place finish the following week at Darlington allowed Johnson to further solidify his point lead over Edwards.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2013_NASCAR_Sprint_All-Star_Race" title="2013 NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race">2013 NASCAR Sprint All-Star Race</a>, Johnson won his record fourth All-Star race after a fast pit stop allowed him to start the final 10-lap sprint in second, and later managed to pass <a href="/wiki/Kasey_Kahne" title="Kasey Kahne">Kasey Kahne</a> for the victory.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> One week later, Johnson finished 22nd after spinning sideways late in the race. At <a href="/wiki/2013_FedEx_400" title="2013 FedEx 400">Dover</a>, Johnson led 143 laps, but finished 17th when he jumped <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">Juan Pablo Montoya</a> on the last restart causing NASCAR to issue him a penalty. He was able to redeem himself for this mistake the following week at Pocono by earning the pole position, leading the most laps, and winning his third race of the season, which increased his point lead to 51 points over Edwards. This also snapped a nine-year winless streak for Johnson at Pocono since sweeping both of the track's 2004 Sprint Cup races. At the <a href="/wiki/2013_Quicken_Loans_400" title="2013 Quicken Loans 400">Quicken Loans 400</a> at Michigan, Johnson closed in on <a href="/wiki/Greg_Biffle" title="Greg Biffle">Greg Biffle</a> for the lead with less than ten laps left, but suffered a flat tire with less than five laps to go. Johnson would finish the race in 28th, his worst finish of the season to that point.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Johnson then finished ninth at Sonoma. At Kentucky, Johnson started third. He had the dominant car of the race, leading 182 of 267 laps. However, on a restart on lap 246, Johnson was slow to get up to speed and was subsequently touched and spun by <a href="/wiki/Joey_Logano" title="Joey Logano">Joey Logano</a>, costing Johnson a shot at the win and giving the race to <a href="/wiki/Matt_Kenseth" title="Matt Kenseth">Matt Kenseth</a>. Johnson was able to charge through the field after the caution and restart to salvage a ninth-place finish.</p>
<p>Returning to Daytona for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Coke_Zero_400" title="2013 Coke Zero 400">Coke Zero 400</a>, Johnson led 94 laps and held off <a href="/wiki/Tony_Stewart" title="Tony Stewart">Tony Stewart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Harvick" title="Kevin Harvick">Kevin Harvick</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Green-white-checker_finish" class="mw-redirect" title="Green-white-checker finish">green-white-checker finish</a> to win his fourth race of the year. In winning the race, Johnson became the first driver since <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Allison" title="Bobby Allison">Bobby Allison</a> in 1982 to sweep both Daytona races in a season.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> This was a significant improvement in Johnson's runs on the restrictor plate tracks, as he had been crashed out of the running at both Daytona races in 2012, had an engine failure early while leading at Talladega in the spring and was part of a crash on the last lap in the fall. Also, he was one of only three drivers to sweep the top ten, the other two drivers being <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Newman" title="Ryan Newman">Ryan Newman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a></p>
<p>At New Hampshire for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Camping_World_RV_Sales_301" title="2013 Camping World RV Sales 301">Camping World RV Sales 301</a>, Johnson qualified second, but failed post-qualifying inspection after his car was found to be too low, and started the race in 43rd,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> the first time in his career he started dead last. In the race, Johnson passed seven cars in the first four laps and reached the Top 20 by lap 50, while reaching the top ten by lap 165; Johnson would finish sixth.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> He almost won the pole position at Indianapolis but was bumped to second by <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Newman" title="Ryan Newman">Ryan Newman</a>. Johnson led the most laps and almost won, but a slow final pit stop cost him the race to Newman. The following week at Pocono, Johnson won another pole position, setting another track qualifying record. He led 43 of the first 80 laps before he cut a right front tire that knocked a spark plug loose and affected the handling of the car. Johnson's pit crew worked hard to repair the car, fixing the plug on the last pit stop, and managing to salvage a 13th-place finish after racing near the back of the pack for most of the race.</p>
<p>Returning to Michigan, Johnson qualified third but crashed in happy hour, forcing him to a backup car and a 43rd starting spot. After running up to the lead through pit stop strategy, Johnson lost an engine on lap 55, relegating him to a 40th-place finish. This was followed by a streak of three poor finishes of 36th at Bristol, 28th at Atlanta, and 40th at Richmond due to crashes and mechanical failures.</p>
<p>Johnson started the Chase seeded in second place. He started the Chase with a fifth place finish at Chicago, followed by a fourth-place finish at New Hampshire. At Dover, Johnson led 243 laps and held off <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a> over the last 25 laps to win his eighth race at the track, also redeeming himself for the restart line violation that had cost him a shot at winning the June race.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Johnson spent the next several races chasing <a href="/wiki/Matt_Kenseth" title="Matt Kenseth">Matt Kenseth</a> for the points lead, eventually gaining it at Talladega, though losing it when he and Kenseth tied for points lead at Martinsville. Returning to Texas, Johnson had the dominant car, leading 255 laps to his sixth win of the season. The following weekend at Phoenix, Johnson avoided trouble in tight racing on two separate occasions (a near scrape in turn 4 on the first lap, and later a near spin after contact with <a href="/wiki/Carl_Edwards" title="Carl Edwards">Carl Edwards</a> in turn 1) to escape with a third-place finish. He also capitalized on Kenseth suffering from a poor-handling car. With Kenseth finishing 23rd, Johnson took a 28-point lead to the season finale at Homestead-Miami Speedway. In the finale, Johnson raced conservatively to a ninth-place finish to secure his sixth title. He closed out the season with six wins, three poles, 16 top five and 24 top ten finishes, with an average finish of 9.8 and average start of 10.7.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Statistically, 2014 was Johnson's worst season to date. He started the season on an up-and-down note, but went winless through the first 11 races of the 2014 season (his best finish was 2nd at Martinsville). Skepticism began to arise, as he had never gone more than 12 races into a season without a win, and hadn't gone that long since the first few years of his Cup career. However, Johnson won the Coca-Cola 600, his first win in the race since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Afterward, he went on to win at Dover the following week, making it the 13th time he had back-to-back wins.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>A few weeks later, Johnson recorded his first win at Michigan, after several years of being deprived of a shot at victory as the result of running out of gas or blowing an engine. However, he didn't keep up with the momentum. After finishing in the top ten at Sonoma and Kentucky, Johnson was collected in an early wreck in the Coke Zero 400, finishing 42nd.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Johnson's streak of misfortune continued the next several weeks, finishing 42nd for the second week in a row at New Hampshire. This was followed up by an inconsistent run at Indy (14th), and poor showings resulting from accidents at Pocono (39th) and Watkins Glen (28th). Despite the poor finishes, Johnson qualified fourth for the Chase.</p>
<p>In the Chase, Johnson finished 12th at Chicagoland, fifth at New Hampshire, and third at Dover to advance to the Contender Round. However, trouble struck when he finished 40th and 17th in the next two races.</p>
<p>At Talladega, Johnson started second and he led a high of 84 laps. However, a 24th-place finish kept him from advancing to the Eliminator Round. At Martinsville, Johnson started seventh but finished 39th after being involved in a crash early in the race. Returning to Texas, Johnson dominated and held off <a href="/wiki/Brad_Keselowski" title="Brad Keselowski">Brad Keselowski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Harvick" title="Kevin Harvick">Kevin Harvick</a> to score his third straight win in the fall Texas race, and also ended an 18-race-winless-streak. At Phoenix, he struggled for most of the day and finished 38th after blowing a tire and crashing out. At the season finale at Homestead, Johnson finished ninth, and closed out finishing 11th in points. This marks the first time in Johnson's Sprint Cup career that he has finished outside of the top ten in the final points.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG/220px-Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG/330px-Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG/440px-Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2968" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Three-wide_multiple_row_back.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson leading the <a href="/wiki/2015_Daytona_500" title="2015 Daytona 500">2015 Daytona 500</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Johnson began his season with a win in the <a href="/wiki/Budweiser_Duel" class="mw-redirect" title="Budweiser Duel">Budweiser Duel</a>. He started the season by finishing fifth in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Daytona_500" title="2015 Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a> for the second year in a row. The following week, he won the <a href="/wiki/2015_Folds_of_Honor_QuikTrip_500" title="2015 Folds of Honor QuikTrip 500">Folds of Honor QuikTrip 500</a> at Atlanta.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Las Vegas, Johnson crashed twice into the outside wall, leaving him with a 41st-place finish. He managed to rebound with an 11th-place finish in Phoenix and a ninth-place finish at California, his first top ten there in two years. At Martinsville, he struggled to a 35th-place finish. However, his momentum returned at Texas when he managed to hold off <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Harvick" title="Kevin Harvick">Kevin Harvick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a> to win. At Bristol, he avoided tight trouble early in the race and managed to come home second to polesitter <a href="/wiki/Matt_Kenseth" title="Matt Kenseth">Matt Kenseth</a>. At Richmond, he finished third. These finishes moved him back up to fourth in the standings. At Talladega, Johnson started fifth and led 50 laps, only to finish second to Earnhardt, Jr.</p>
<p>At Kansas, Johnson gambled by staying out on the last round of pit stops, and held off Harvick and Earnhardt again to win his third race at Kansas and of the season. In winning, he established a Cup record of 23 wins on 1.5-mile tracks, taking what was both his 200th top five and his 300th top ten finish.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> At Charlotte, he spun out on two occasions. The first time was early in the race while running 16th coming out of turn 4 but he was lucky to avoid hitting anything. He wasn't so lucky on the second spin late in the race; while running fifth, he spun out again at the exact same place, and hit the wall in pit road, causing some nose damage. Those spin-outs would leave him with a 40th-place finish. He rebounded the following week with a <a href="/wiki/2015_FedEx_400" title="2015 FedEx 400">win at Dover</a>, and also became one of four drivers to have won 10 or more races at one track. This gave him a total of 74 career wins, two fewer than <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a>'s 76.</p>
<p>At Pocono, Johnson cut a tire on lap 88, but did not take major damage. He was able to work his way through the field to finish in third place. He finished 19th at Michigan after the race was called for rain on lap 138. At Sonoma, Johnson led the most laps at 45 laps, but a late race caution caused by <a href="/wiki/Casey_Mears" title="Casey Mears">Casey Mears</a>' broken wheel axle cost him, and he was passed by <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Busch" title="Kyle Busch">Kyle Busch</a> with five laps to go, and slipped back to sixth place.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg/250px-TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg" width="250" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg/375px-TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg/500px-TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3128" data-file-height="1448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TSM350_-_2015_-_Jimmie_Johnson_2_-_Stierch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson during <a href="/wiki/2015_Toyota/Save_Mart_350" title="2015 Toyota/Save Mart 350">2015 Toyota/Save Mart 350</a> qualifying</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Returning to Daytona, Johnson started 12th and led 35 laps before finishing second to <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a>, in a repeat of the Talladega race. At Kentucky, Johnson started sixth and ran inside the top ten for most of the night, finishing ninth. At the second stop in Pocono, Johnson, along with two of his Hendrick teammates, Jeff Gordon, and Dale Earnhardt, Jr, took advantage of several cars running out of fuel to finish in the Top 6 (Gordon finished 3rd, Dale Jr. took 4th, Johnson grabbed 6th). At Watkins Glen, despite suffering two penalties (lap 3: Overshooting the entrance to the inner loop, and caution No. 1 (lap 26-28): Speeding through pit road) Johnson rallied to finish 10th. He wasn't so lucky at Michigan; late in the race, he got loose and spun in turn 3, and damaged the splitter on his car, resulting in a 39th place finish (10 laps down). He rebounded at Bristol by finishing 4th, but had bad luck once more at Darlington. He spun out on lap 134 in turn 4, bringing out the 7th caution, and was never a real threat. He ended up 19th. He was able to recover a bit for a 9th place finish at Richmond, and started 1st in the Chase in a three-way-tie between him, Kyle Busch, and Matt Kenseth.</p>
<p>Johnson opened up the Chase in a rough way. At Chicagoland, he blew a left front tire early in the race, but was able to charge through the field to salvage an 11th place finish. He also was the subject of controversy when he made contact with <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Harvick" title="Kevin Harvick">Kevin Harvick</a> on a three-wide pass that led to Harvick cutting a left rear tire, leaving Harvick with a 42nd place finish.</p>
<p>At Loudon, Johnson finished 6th after blowing a tire in the 3rd position. At Dover, his Chase hopes came to an end when his car broke a drive line, leading him to finish 36 laps down in 41st place. At the fall race at Texas Johnson won, passing Brad Keselowski with 4 laps to go. This marked his fourth consecutive win in the fall race, and third consecutive win on that track, having also won the spring race. That victory also marked the 75th of his Sprint Cup Series career, putting him one race win short of tying Dale Earnhardt's career wins. Also in the process, he snapped a 20-race-winless-streak.</p>
<p>Johnson finished 5th at Phoenix, and for the third year in a row, he finished 9th at Homestead. Also in the process, he beat Ryan Newman by 1 point to finish 10th in the final standings. With the retirement of his teammate and mentor, Jeff Gordon, Johnson assumed the active wins record with 75.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016:_The_seventh_title">2016: The seventh title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2016: The seventh title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Johnson began the 2016 season with a 16th place finish at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Daytona_500" title="2016 Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a>. In the next race at Atlanta Motor Speedway, he won his 1st race of the season and the 76th of his career, tying the late <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a> for seventh on the all-time wins list.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Johnson finished third and eleventh in the next two events of the season at Las Vegas and Phoenix. His second victory of the season came in the fifth race, the <a href="/wiki/2016_Auto_Club_400" title="2016 Auto Club 400">Auto Club 400</a>, where Johnson passed Harvick in an overtime finish.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It was also the first time since 2011 that he finished in the top five at the Auto Club Speedway. In the <a href="/wiki/2016_STP_500" title="2016 STP 500">STP 500</a> at Martinsville Speedway, Johnson recorded a 9th-place finish after moving through the field after qualifying 24th.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> One week later, Johnson finished fourth in the <a href="/wiki/2016_Duck_Commander_500" title="2016 Duck Commander 500">Duck Commander 500</a> at Texas Motor Speedway despite suffering minor damage during a 13-car accident that occurred within 50 laps of the finish.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2016_Food_City_500" title="2016 Food City 500">Food City 500</a> at Bristol, Johnson finished 23rd after making an unscheduled pit stop due to a loose lug nut on lap 300. At Richmond, he led 44 laps early in the race and finished 3rd. At <a href="/wiki/2016_GEICO_500" title="2016 GEICO 500">Talladega</a>, Johnson was spun by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Menard" title="Paul Menard">Paul Menard</a> and got involved in a multi-car accident with 28 laps to go, finishing 22nd. Johnson's streak of misfortune continued through the next several months, crashing out at <a href="/wiki/2016_AAA_400_Drive_for_Autism" title="2016 AAA 400 Drive for Autism">Dover</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_Axalta_%22We_Paint_Winners%22_400" title="2016 Axalta &quot;We Paint Winners&quot; 400">Pocono</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_Coke_Zero_400" title="2016 Coke Zero 400">Daytona</a>, Kentucky and at Watkins Glen, where he finished last for the first time in his career. His top-10 finishes during the period came only in the <a href="/wiki/2016_Coca-Cola_600" title="2016 Coca-Cola 600">Coca-Cola 600</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_Brickyard_400" title="2016 Brickyard 400">Brickyard 400</a>, where he finished 3rd in both races. Johnson finished 7th and 6th at Bristol and Michigan the following two weeks, but finished 33rd at Darlington after he spun out of turn 4. Johnson then finished 11th at Richmond. He qualified 8th for the Chase.</p>
<p>Johnson began the <a href="/wiki/Chase_for_the_Sprint_Cup" title="Chase for the Sprint Cup">The Chase for the Sprint Cup</a> by leading a race-high 118 laps at Chicagoland, but received a speeding penalty during a green flag pit stop late in the race, ultimately finished 12th. Johnson finished 8th the following week at Loudon. At <a href="/wiki/2016_Citizen_Soldier_400" title="2016 Citizen Soldier 400">Dover</a>, Johnson led 90 laps but once again received a pit road penalty with 105 laps to go, costing him a win. He would charge through the field and finish 7th (1st car a lap down). He was able to move to the "Round of 12" of the Chase.</p>
<p>At Charlotte, Johnson led a race-high 155 laps and won the <a href="/wiki/2016_Bank_of_America_500" title="2016 Bank of America 500">Bank of America 500</a>, claiming his 8th win at the track and the 3rd win of the season, also snapping his 24-race winless streak. This is the first time he advances to the "Round of 8" under the current Chase system. He then finished 4th at Kansas and 23rd at <a href="/wiki/2016_Hellmann%27s_500" title="2016 Hellmann's 500">Talladega</a>. At Martinsville, Jimmie had contact with <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hamlin" title="Denny Hamlin">Denny Hamlin</a> on lap 198 and had a tire rub to cause a caution but was able to stay on the lead lap. Later during a caution on lap 362, he lost fuel pressure but was able to get the car refired and stayed on the lead lap again. After the restart, he took the lead from <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hamlin" title="Denny Hamlin">Denny Hamlin</a> and led the final 92 laps to win the <a href="/wiki/2016_Goody%27s_Fast_Relief_500" title="2016 Goody's Fast Relief 500">Goody's Fast Relief 500</a>. He would be able to advance to the "Championship 4" and race for the Championship at Homestead. Johnson finished 11th in the rain-shortened race at <a href="/wiki/2016_AAA_Texas_500" title="2016 AAA Texas 500">Texas</a>, and 38th at <a href="/wiki/2016_Can-Am_500" title="2016 Can-Am 500">Phoenix</a> after being penalized a lap for passing the pace car coming down to pit road and involved in a wreck on a restart.</p>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" width="40" height="22" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="759" data-file-height="415" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Jimmie_Johnson_wins_seventh_NASCAR_Cup_Series_championship" class="extiw" title="wikinews:Jimmie Johnson wins seventh NASCAR Cup Series championship">Jimmie Johnson wins seventh NASCAR Cup Series championship</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Johnson claimed his seventh championship with a victory at <a href="/wiki/2016_Ford_EcoBoost_400" title="2016 Ford EcoBoost 400">Homestead</a> on November 20. After losing his starting spot due to a pre-race inspection fault, Johnson started at the rear of the field. He progressed though the field, being in the top 10 for most of the race. On a late race restart, fellow contender Carl Edwards came across the nose of Joey Logano, hit the inside wall and triggered a huge wreck, ending Edwards' championship hopes. Johnson was able to avoid the accident, and was put into position to win the title. On the final restart, he passed <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Larson" title="Kyle Larson">Kyle Larson</a> to win the race and claim his seventh championship, tying with <a href="/wiki/Richard_Petty" title="Richard Petty">Richard Petty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a> for the most all-time of championships.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_of_Champions">Race of Champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Race of Champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg/200px-Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg/300px-Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg/400px-Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Johnson_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson driving a Fiat Grande Punto S2000 Abarth at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Race_of_Champions" title="2007 Race of Champions">2007 Race of Champions</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Johnson first raced in the <a href="/wiki/Race_of_Champions" title="Race of Champions">Race of Champions</a> in Europe in <a href="/wiki/2002_Race_of_Champions" title="2002 Race of Champions">2002</a>. He was eliminated in the first runoff by then <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">world rally champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm" title="Marcus Grönholm">Marcus Grönholm</a> of <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> but he and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colin_Edwards" title="Colin Edwards">Colin Edwards</a> racing as Team USA won the teams' championship. He returned to the event two years later but lost the quarter finals 0–2 to <a href="/wiki/Mattias_Ekstr%C3%B6m" title="Mattias Ekström">Mattias Ekström</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> who was <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Tourenwagen_Masters" title="Deutsche Tourenwagen Masters">DTM German Touring Car</a> champion that year.</p>
<p>Johnson entered the 2006 event but did not start due to injury received just days before the race.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> He still attended the event to cheer for teammate <a href="/wiki/Travis_Pastrana" title="Travis Pastrana">Travis Pastrana</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2007_Race_of_Champions" title="2007 Race of Champions">2007 event</a> Johnson was eliminated before the quarter-finals by <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">F1</a> driver <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Bourdais" title="Sébastien Bourdais">Sébastien Bourdais</a> of France.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand-Am">Grand-Am</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Grand-Am">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, he began his Grand-Am career in the Rolex 24 at Daytona, where he finished eighth. He also entered the event one year later, which his team, <a href="/wiki/Howard-Boss_Motorsports" class="mw-redirect" title="Howard-Boss Motorsports">Howard-Boss Motorsports</a>, managed to finish second. Two years later, he entered two events, which were both held at <a href="/wiki/Daytona_International_Speedway" title="Daytona International Speedway">Daytona International Speedway</a>. During the races, his team finished 9th and 19th. In 2008, Johnson moved to <a href="/wiki/Bob_Stallings_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Stallings Racing">Bob Stallings Racing</a> with <a href="/wiki/Alex_Gurney" title="Alex Gurney">Alex Gurney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jon_Fogarty" title="Jon Fogarty">Jon Fogarty</a> to race in the 2008 Rolex 24 at Daytona, where the team finished second. One year later, he returned with <a href="/wiki/GAINSCO/Bob_Stallings_Racing" title="GAINSCO/Bob Stallings Racing">GAINSCO/Bob Stallings Racing</a> for his fifth Rolex 24 appearance. During the race, his team managed to finish seventh. He returned to the team in 2010, to race in the Rolex 24 and Sahlen's Six Hours of the Glen.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> During the Rolex 24 at Daytona his team finished 21st,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> while at Watkins Glen the team managed to finish sixth.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> He returned to the Rolex 24, in 2011 where his team managed to finish 15th.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg/200px-Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg/300px-Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg/400px-Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chandra_Johnson_-_Jimmie_Johnson_-_Barack_Obama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Johnson (center) with his wife Chandra and President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Johnson was born on September 17, 1975<sup id="cite_ref-hendrickbiography_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hendrickbiography-1">[1]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/El_Cajon,_California" title="El Cajon, California">El Cajon, California</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> the son of Catherine Ellen "Cathy" (née Dunnill) and Gary Ernest Johnson.<sup id="cite_ref-family_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-family-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> He has two younger brothers, <a href="/wiki/Jarit_Johnson" title="Jarit Johnson">Jarit</a> and Jessie. Both have made professional off-road racing starts in the <a href="/wiki/TORC:_The_Off_Road_Championship" title="TORC: The Off Road Championship">TORC: The Off Road Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Johnson attended <a href="/wiki/Granite_Hills_High_School_(El_Cajon,_California)" title="Granite Hills High School (El Cajon, California)">Granite Hills High School</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-foundationaboutus_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundationaboutus-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> while he raced motorcycles during the weekends. He was a varsity water polo player, diver and swimmer and graduated in 1993. The number 48 is retired from all sports teams uniforms at his school and Johnson was inducted into the school's Athletic Hall of Fame.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Johnson lives in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a><sup id="cite_ref-hendrickbiography_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hendrickbiography-1">[1]</a></sup> like many other NASCAR drivers. He is married to Chandra Janway, the two having known each other since 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> They have two daughters, Genevieve and Lydia.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Jimmie_Johnson_Foundation">The Jimmie Johnson Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The Jimmie Johnson Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Jimmie Johnson Foundation was launched by Johnson and his wife, Chandra, in 2006. The foundation helps children, families, and communities in need. In 2007, Johnson opened Jimmie Johnson's Victory Lanes in <a href="/wiki/Randleman,_North_Carolina" title="Randleman, North Carolina">Randleman, North Carolina</a>, which is a four-lane bowling alley for campers at Pattie and Kyle Petty's Victory Junction Gang Camp. The foundation supports several charities, including <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity" title="Habitat for Humanity">Habitat for Humanity</a>, Hendrick Marrow Program, <a href="/wiki/Make-A-Wish_Foundation" title="Make-A-Wish Foundation">Make-A-Wish Foundation</a>, and Victory Junction. Every year, it holds a golf tournament in San Diego,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> which raises money for K-12 public education. Since the beginning, the tournament has raised a total of eight million US$ to help fund several projects. During 2009 and 2010, the foundation awarded $1.5 million for the Education Champions Grants program. The money is given to public schools in California, Oklahoma, and North Carolina. It helps fund basic needs, such as technology, outdoor classrooms, playground construction, and reading programs. The foundation has also assisted the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> with disaster relief efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-teamlowesjimmie_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamlowesjimmie-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foundationaboutus_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundationaboutus-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Johnson joined the <a href="/wiki/Ban_Bossy" title="Ban Bossy">Ban Bossy</a> campaign, as a spokesperson advocating leadership in young girls.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYPost1_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYPost1-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYDNews1_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYDNews1-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_achievements">Career achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Career achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Johnson has won the <a href="/wiki/Driver_of_the_Year" title="Driver of the Year">Driver of the Year</a> Award five times (2006, 2007, 2009, 2010, 2013). In 2009, he became the first racing driver to win the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press_Male_Athlete_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Associated Press Male Athlete of the Year">Associated Press Male Athlete of the Year</a> Award in the United States.</p>
<p>Johnson was ranked No. 1 on <a href="/wiki/Forbes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes.com">Forbes.com</a>'s list of "Most Influential Athletes" for two consecutive years (2011, 2012).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_and_milestones">Records and milestones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Records and milestones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With 80 career points-paying victories, Johnson is the winningest active driver, sixth place among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_all-time_NASCAR_Cup_Series_winners" title="List of all-time NASCAR Cup Series winners">all-time NASCAR Cup Series winners</a>; and ranked third among those who have competed during the sport's modern era (1972–present).</p>
<p>Johnson is the all-time winningest Cup Series driver at the following tracks:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Auto_Club_Speedway" title="Auto Club Speedway">Auto Club Speedway</a> (6)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Motor_Speedway" title="Charlotte Motor Speedway">Charlotte Motor Speedway</a> (8)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dover_International_Speedway" title="Dover International Speedway">Dover International Speedway</a> (10)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kansas_Speedway" title="Kansas Speedway">Kansas Speedway</a> (3, tied with Jeff Gordon)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Motor_Speedway" title="Las Vegas Motor Speedway">Las Vegas Motor Speedway</a> (4)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Texas_Motor_Speedway" title="Texas Motor Speedway">Texas Motor Speedway</a> (6)</li>
</ul>
<p>Johnson has won a Cup Series race at every track except <a href="/wiki/Chicagoland_Speedway" title="Chicagoland Speedway">Chicagoland Speedway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Speedway" title="Kentucky Speedway">Kentucky Speedway</a> (2011- ), and <a href="/wiki/Watkins_Glen_International" title="Watkins Glen International">Watkins Glen International</a>.</p>
<p>Johnson is the only driver to have qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Chase_for_the_Sprint_Cup" title="Chase for the Sprint Cup">Chase for the Sprint Cup</a> every single year since its inception in <a href="/wiki/2004_Chase_for_the_NEXTEL_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Chase for the NEXTEL Cup">2004</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television_appearances">Film and television appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Film and television appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Johnson made an appearance as himself in the 2005 film <i><a href="/wiki/Herbie:_Fully_Loaded" title="Herbie: Fully Loaded">Herbie: Fully Loaded</a></i>.</p>
<p>Johnson starred in an episode of the television series <i><a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_(TV_series)" title="Las Vegas (TV series)">Las Vegas</a></i> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>Johnson starred in an episode of the <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> reality television series <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=24/7_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="24/7 (TV series) (page does not exist)">24/7</a></i>, titled "Jimmie Johnson: Race to Daytona". Cameras followed him from January 2010 to the <a href="/wiki/2010_Daytona_500" title="2010 Daytona 500">52nd Daytona 500</a> held on February 14.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Johnson appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i> during its <a href="/wiki/List_of_The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show_episodes_Season_10_(2012%E2%80%9313)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of The Ellen DeGeneres Show episodes Season 10 (2012–13)">tenth season</a> in 2013. Fresh off his second <a href="/wiki/2013_Daytona_500" title="2013 Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a> victory, Johnson challenged host <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> to a go-kart race.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 19, 2013, Johnson became the first professional athlete to co-host <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>'s flagship news show, <i><a href="/wiki/SportsCenter" title="SportsCenter">SportsCenter</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Johnson appeared on the series <i><a href="/wiki/Repeat_After_Me_(TV_series)" title="Repeat After Me (TV series)">Repeat After Me</a></i> and voiced a lobster named Jimmie on the animated kids show <i><a href="/wiki/Bubble_Guppies" title="Bubble Guppies">Bubble Guppies</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazines">Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Johnson has appeared on the cover of several magazines, including <i>NASCAR Illustrated</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Men%27s_Fitness" title="Men's Fitness">Men's Fitness</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Success_(magazine)" title="Success (magazine)">Success</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Johnson makes a cameo appearance as a pilot in the music video for <a href="/wiki/The_Avett_Brothers" title="The Avett Brothers">The Avett Brothers</a>' "Ain't No Man," the lead single from the album <i><a href="/wiki/True_Sadness" title="True Sadness">True Sadness</a></i> (2016).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Johnson's Cup ride, the No. 48 Lowe's Chevrolet, is featured on the covers of <i><a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Racing_2003_Season" title="NASCAR Racing 2003 Season">NASCAR Racing 2003 Season</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/NASCAR_The_Game:_2011" title="NASCAR The Game: 2011">NASCAR The Game: 2011</a></i>.</p>
<p>Johnson and <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Motorsports" title="Hendrick Motorsports">Hendrick Motorsports</a> teammate <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a> are featured on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/NASCAR_06:_Total_Team_Control" title="NASCAR 06: Total Team Control">NASCAR 06: Total Team Control</a></i>, highlighting Team Control, the main addition of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Johnson is also one of the six cover drivers of <i><a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Kart_Racing" title="NASCAR Kart Racing">NASCAR Kart Racing</a></i>.</p>
<p>Johnson is featured in the 2011 racing video game <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Johnson%27s_Anything_with_an_Engine" title="Jimmie Johnson's Anything with an Engine">Jimmie Johnson's Anything with an Engine</a></i>.</p>
<p>Johnson is featured as a playable driver in <i><a href="/wiki/Forza_Motorsport_6" title="Forza Motorsport 6">Forza Motorsport 6</a></i>, via the NASCAR expansion pack.<sup id="cite_ref-Forza_Motorsport_6_NASCAR_Expansion_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forza_Motorsport_6_NASCAR_Expansion-109">[109]</a></sup> The expansion features twenty-four paint schemes from the <a href="/wiki/2016_NASCAR_Sprint_Cup_Series" title="2016 NASCAR Sprint Cup Series">2016 Sprint Cup Series season</a>, including Johnson's No. 48 Lowe's SS.<sup id="cite_ref-Forza_Motorsport_6_NASCAR_Expansion_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forza_Motorsport_6_NASCAR_Expansion-109">[109]</a></sup> Johnson, along with <a href="/wiki/Chase_Elliott" title="Chase Elliott">Chase Elliott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Busch" title="Kyle Busch">Kyle Busch</a>, provide commentary in the expansion as the "voices of motorsport."<sup id="cite_ref-Forza_Motorsport_6_NASCAR_Expansion_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forza_Motorsport_6_NASCAR_Expansion-109">[109]</a></sup> Johnson and Elliott also had roles in developing the expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsports_career_results">Motorsports career results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmie_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Motorsports career results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
